  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_42024edf-cebc-4b9a-9011-2746829cacd2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer7791391595688325007">Dear Reader,<br/><br/>I hope, for your sake, that you have not chosen to read this book because you are in the mood for a pleasant experience. If this is the case, I advise you to put this book down instantaneously, because of all the books describing the unhappy lives of the Baudelaire orphans, The Miserable Mill might be the unhappiest yet. Violet, Klaus, and Sunny Baudelaire are </span>
  <span id="freeText7791391595688325007" style="display:none">Dear Reader,<br /><br />I hope, for your sake, that you have not chosen to read this book because you are in the mood for a pleasant experience. If this is the case, I advise you to put this book down instantaneously, because of all the books describing the unhappy lives of the Baudelaire orphans, The Miserable Mill might be the unhappiest yet. Violet, Klaus, and Sunny Baudelaire are sent to Paltryville to work in a lumber mill, and they find disaster and misfortune lurking behind every log.<br /><br />The pages of this book, I'm sorry to inform you, contain such unpleasantries as a giant pincher machine, a bad casserole, a man with a cloud of smoke where his head should be, a hypnotist, a terrible accident resulting in injury, and coupons.<br /><br />I have promised to write down the entire history of these three poor children, but you haven't, so if you prefer stories that are more heartwarming, please feel free to make another selection.<br /><br />With all due respect,<br /><br />Lemony Snicket</span>

<div id="review_2455854496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2455854496" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2455854496?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=middle-grade-children-s">middle-grade-children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2455854496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer710753892794144620">The children head to Paltryville where they'll meet there new guardian. They arrive at the Lucky Smells Lumbermill where they meet Sir, the owner of the mill. Sir is the Baudelaire's new guardian and the children learn that the mill will be there new place of employment. Once again, the children are told not to worry about Count Olaf and that they'll be kept safe from him.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"The deal is this: I will try to make sure that Count Olaf and his associates never go anywhere near you, and you will wor</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText710753892794144620" style="display:none">The children head to Paltryville where they'll meet there new guardian. They arrive at the Lucky Smells Lumbermill where they meet Sir, the owner of the mill. Sir is the Baudelaire's new guardian and the children learn that the mill will be there new place of employment. Once again, the children are told not to worry about Count Olaf and that they'll be kept safe from him.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"The deal is this: I will try to make sure that Count Olaf and his associates never go anywhere near you, and you will work in my lumbermill until you come of age and get all that money. Is that a fair deal?"</b>
</i><br /><br />Life at the lumber mill is horrible. They're barely given any food to eat and they're forced to work very difficult and dangerous jobs. Not only that, they're paid with coupons they can't even use! Klaus ends up getting hurt which breaks his glasses, and when he returns from the doctor he's become hypnotized. It appears that somehow Count Olaf is up to his heinous crimes again. The children discover that Count Olaf has disguised himself as a secretary at the mill and they must find a way to expose him.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Why, hello there, little girls," Count Olaf said in a ridiculously high voice, as if he were really a receptionist named Shirley instead of an evil man after the Baudelaire fortune. "What are your names?"</b>
</i><br /><br />We enjoyed reading this installment in the series, but it was our least favorite yet. Our interests in the themes are sort of getting burned out after reading this book and we decided to take a break before moving on to book five. It just started feeling like the same story over and over again with the repeating plot, but the addition of new characters always makes it interesting. I will say that the books do seem to be getting darker and darker as they go on, not only that, larger with more pages. It's fun to see what tricks Count Olaf will be up to next, but I'm still wondering why he keeps coming around to steal the children when the money isn't even available until Violet turns 18!<br /><br />My kids are still enjoying the series and we plan to finish all the books. After our break, we started book five, and it's promising so far.<br /><br />4****</span>
  <a data-text-id="710753892794144620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_948308443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/948308443" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/948308443?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer948308443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1538200061297357658">The Miserable Mill continues the trend of me liking each book less than the previous one in this series. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong - it's still a fun read with plenty of cleverness and wit, and Celyn still seems to be enjoying me reading her the stories. It's also worth noting that this volume has the lowest average rating on Goodreads of all 13 books in the series, so I'm hopeful things will improve. <br/><br/>In this book the established formula is applied with little or no variation. The bad point, for me, th</span>
  <span id="freeText1538200061297357658" style="display:none">The Miserable Mill continues the trend of me liking each book less than the previous one in this series. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong - it's still a fun read with plenty of cleverness and wit, and Celyn still seems to be enjoying me reading her the stories. It's also worth noting that this volume has the lowest average rating on Goodreads of all 13 books in the series, so I'm hopeful things will improve. <br /><br />In this book the established formula is applied with little or no variation. The bad point, for me, though was the descent into truly cartoon writing. In all the books before the world was similar to ours, bizarre, but largely believable. Normal laws of physics applies, things were internally consistent.<br /><br />In The Miserable Mill many things are wholly surreal and/or plain don't make sense.<br /><br />Some random examples:<br /><br />i) The signs being made out of chewed up chewing gum ... why?<br /><br />ii) The Boss having no name and his face being wholly concealed by smoke from his cigar the entire time - that steps into a kind of silly that is very different from the previous books' silliness. I cannot see in my mind a cloud of smoke from a cigar that is totally impenetrable and moves with someone.<br /><br />iii) A log being sawed is moved from its path (where it is held by the fact the circular saw is halfway through its length) by a child with a strip of metal using only the force that can be applied through the adhesion of a piece of chewing gum stuck to both the log and the metal strip.<br /><br />iv) A baby has a lengthy 'sword fight' with a grown and murderous woman. The woman is using a sword and the baby ... is using her teeth. We are repeatedly told that the teeth and sword clash.<br /><br />If the books had begun like this I would be ok with us being in a cartoonish world where that kind of thing happens (though I still wouldn't be able to visualize the sword fight in any satisfactory manner). But the first three books aren't like that (though they do move slowly in that direction) and in book 4 is comes as an unwelcome non sequitur. <br /><br /> You should join my 3-emails-a-year mailing list for updates about my books. #prizes <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1">http://eepurl.com/cimnK1</a><br /><br /><br />....</span>
  <a data-text-id="1538200061297357658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237009861" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237009861?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=beautifully-written">beautifully-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237009861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13317319930450675307">This is perhaps the most anxiety-inducing book in the most anxiety-inducing series of all time.<br/><br/>There is something about the particular Count Olaf evil plan hijinks in this book that is SO MUCH WORSE to me than all the others?? It’s not so much “fun villainy” to me as it is “extremely stressful stuff of nightmares.”<br/><br/>So not necessarily the most consistently pleasant reading experience.<br/><br/>HOWEVER there is a really cool part of this book! The Baudelaire orphans, up to this point, have very narrow and co</span>
  <span id="freeText13317319930450675307" style="display:none">This is perhaps the most anxiety-inducing book in the most anxiety-inducing series of all time.<br /><br />There is something about the particular Count Olaf evil plan hijinks in this book that is SO MUCH WORSE to me than all the others?? It’s not so much “fun villainy” to me as it is “extremely stressful stuff of nightmares.”<br /><br />So not necessarily the most consistently pleasant reading experience.<br /><br />HOWEVER there is a really cool part of this book! The Baudelaire orphans, up to this point, have very narrow and consistent, like, specializations? What do you call the constant semi-adult-ish habits and passions of a child I do not know. Anyway: Violet invents, Klaus reads, Sunny bites.<br /><br />In this book, <i>Violet</i> reads! And Klaus invents! It’s kind of a fun thing of, like, hey children of the world, you do not need to limit yourself. You can be good at a lot of things, even if someone is better at them than you. Woohoo!<br /><br />Count Olaf’s role in this book is very limited, and therefore not as AMAZING as he normally is in the other books (villain-wise). But there are some great characters in this one! I love Phil. Also there is a gay partnership in this book and no one can tell me otherwise and so there.<br /><br />Bottom line: Not the best book in this series. Maybe the worst? But still fabulouswonderfulamazingIlovethisworldsomuchohmygod.<br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6700023823066930429"><b>The Miserable Mill (Series of Unfortunate Events #4), Lemony Snicket</b><br/><br/>The Miserable Mill is the fourth novel of the children's novel series A Series of Unfortunate Events by Lemony Snicket. In this novel, the Baudelaire orphans live with the owner of Lucky Smells Lumber Mill. The book was published on April 15, 2000, by HarperCollins and illustrated by Brett Helquist.<br/><br/>Violet, Klaus and Sunny Baudelaire are traveling on a train heading for Paltryville, the location of the children's new home, the Lu</span>
  <span id="freeText6700023823066930429" style="display:none"><b>The Miserable Mill (Series of Unfortunate Events #4), Lemony Snicket</b><br /><br />The Miserable Mill is the fourth novel of the children's novel series A Series of Unfortunate Events by Lemony Snicket. In this novel, the Baudelaire orphans live with the owner of Lucky Smells Lumber Mill. The book was published on April 15, 2000, by HarperCollins and illustrated by Brett Helquist.<br /><br />Violet, Klaus and Sunny Baudelaire are traveling on a train heading for Paltryville, the location of the children's new home, the Lucky Smells Lumbermill.<br /><br />Upon arrival, the children learn that they will have to work at the mill, but as part of the deal, their new guardian, Sir (they call him Sir because his name is so long that nobody pronounces it right), will try to keep Count Olaf, their nemesis, away. They meet Sir's more sympathetic partner, Charles, who shows them the library, which contains three books, one about the history of the lumbermill, one about the town constitution, and one donated by Dr. Georgina Orwell, the local optometrist, who lives in an eye-shaped building, which also resembles, suspiciously, the tattoo on their nemesis, Count Olaf's, ankle.<br /><br />Klaus breaks his own glasses when he is purposely tripped by the new foreman, Flacutono, and is sent to see Dr. Orwell. When Klaus returns from the optometrist, hours later, he acts strangely, as if in a trance. The next day in the lumbermill, Flacutono instructs Klaus to operate a stamping machine. Klaus causes an accident by dropping the machine on Phil, an optimistic coworker. Flacutono exclaims that the machine "cost an inordinate amount of money". The other workers ask what the unfamiliar word means and Klaus defines the word. Klaus explains that he doesn't remember what happened between when he broke his glasses and waking up in the mill. Foreman Flacutono trips him again, once again causing his glasses to break. This time though, Violet and Sunny accompany Klaus to Dr. Orwell's office.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز نوزدهم ماه آوریل سال 2011میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: کارگاه مصیبت بار؛ نویسنده: لمونی اسنیکت؛ مترجم: زهرا زرکش؛ تهران، انتشارات ماهی؛ 1381؛ در 164ص؛ شابک: 9649333304؛ فروست: مجموعه ماجراهای بچه‌‌ های بدشانس کتاب چهارم؛ چاپ دوم 1383؛ سوم 1384؛ چهارم 1386؛ پنجم 1387؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /><br />بچه ها به کارگاه چوب بری «لاکی اسملز» می‌روند، و سخت کار می‌کنند؛ آنها با «فلیپ»، یک مرد خوشبین، و «چارلز» یک مرد مهربان، آشنا می‌شوند، اما رییس کارگاه، از آنها بیگاری می‌کشد، و سرپرست کارگران نیز، همدست «کنت الاف» است، که با نقشه ای از طریق هیپنوتیزم می‌خواهد که ثروت آنها به دست آورد، اما دوباره شکست میخورد؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 06/08/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

Perhaps if I did, I would like them better now but unfortunately I feel lukewarm at best about this series. I just feel like these stories go around and around in circles and I'm quite tired of it. I like the kids but the story just isn't working for me anymore. This was probably my least favourite book so far but thinking about it now, the mill was probably one of the stronger st</span>
  <span id="freeText4856018124542660009" style="display:none">The more books I read, the less I like this series. I'm now 100% positive that I didn't read these books as a child. Perhaps if I did, I would like them better now but unfortunately I feel lukewarm at best about this series. I just feel like these stories go around and around in circles and I'm quite tired of it. I like the kids but the story just isn't working for me anymore. This was probably my least favourite book so far but thinking about it now, the mill was probably one of the stronger stories. <br /><br />I will probably return to this series eventually and I plan to watch the Netflix show to see if I like it any better but for now, I'm done reading this series. <br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~ <br /><br />“A new experience can be extremely pleasurable, or extremely irritating, or somewhere in between, and you never know until you try it out.”</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16087601459931897990">This series just gets more and more miserable as it goes along and I just love it! It still truly astonishes me how horrible the adults in these books are no matter how many times I read them. The way they treat the children is absolutely appalling but I think that's part of the charm of this series. The poor Baudelaires can just never get a break! That's what makes this series real though because a lot of the time in real life, orphans do have terrible experiences and bounce around from home to</span>
  <span id="freeText16087601459931897990" style="display:none">This series just gets more and more miserable as it goes along and I just love it! It still truly astonishes me how horrible the adults in these books are no matter how many times I read them. The way they treat the children is absolutely appalling but I think that's part of the charm of this series. The poor Baudelaires can just never get a break! That's what makes this series real though because a lot of the time in real life, orphans do have terrible experiences and bounce around from home to home. I really enjoyed my reread of this book, and although this book as a whole is not my favourite of the series, Count Olaf's disguise in this one is my favourite out of all of them! </span>

<div id="review_309152372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309152372" />
    <a title="Georgina Ortiz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7387625-georgina-ortiz"><img alt="Georgina Ortiz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327892842p2/7387625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309152372?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Georgina Ortiz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Georgina Ortiz" href="/user/show/7387625-georgina-ortiz">Georgina Ortiz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309152372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15326431438806003300">Favorite insight: <i>It is much, much worse to receive bad news through the written word than by somebody simply telling you, and I'm sure you understand why. When somebody simply tells you bad news, you hear it once, and that's the end of it. But when bad news is written down, whether in a letter or a newspaper or on your arm in felt tip pen, each time you read it, you feel as if you are receiving the news again and again.</i></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17123760302431683685">After reading Lemony Snicket's 'the Dark' I decided to try the Unfortunate events series again. It started out ok and I simply can't believe how ridiculous and outlandish it was. I can handle fantasy, but I like it to be rooted in some sort of reality. I then read that many readers consider this the worst book in the series. I can agree with that so far. I will give another one a go.<br/><br/>Examples. It was the end that was so beyond silly. Sunny, the baby, had a sword fight with her teeth. Claus can ma</span>
  <span id="freeText17123760302431683685" style="display:none">After reading Lemony Snicket's 'the Dark' I decided to try the Unfortunate events series again. It started out ok and I simply can't believe how ridiculous and outlandish it was. I can handle fantasy, but I like it to be rooted in some sort of reality. I then read that many readers consider this the worst book in the series. I can agree with that so far. I will give another one a go.<br /><br />Examples. It was the end that was so beyond silly. Sunny, the baby, had a sword fight with her teeth. Claus can make a whole invention in less than a second while someone is on the lumber saw about to be sewn in half. We all know the adults in this story are idiots really. This was simply silly.<br /><br />I am not much of a fan of this book. I also realize much of the book is taken up with explaining things and not action. It is very simple really without all the explaining. I felt this was a bad entry in the series. It's hard for the all to be great. </span>

<div id="review_47696671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47696671" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47696671?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47696671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9301285928837995728">Miserable indeed. Unfortunately this book in <i>A Series of Unfortunate Events</i> takes its title too literally. I enjoyed the first book and love the concept of put-upon children succeeding with no foreseeable hope on the horizon. However, the execution is too formulaic, mill-like if you will. I can put up with the repetition, because the author's bits of wit keep it fun, but this had less wit and more formula than the first three. <br/><br/><br/><br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review47696671">

I'm hoping that the 5th redeems the fourth and that it's more exciting than this one was. I did love that Count Olaf was in drag haha I'm interested to see how they adapt this one considering it was kind of boring and really felt like a filler book to be honest. I still enjoyed it though. :)<br/><br/>Now on to "The Austere Academy"!! <br/><br/>- Richard</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11025719072639134107"><i>The Miserable Mill</i> is the fourth installment of <i>A Series of Unfortunate Events</i>. A lot happened in this book and I'm still a little shook from it. <br/><br/>Now in this book we still have the three kids: Klaus, Violet, and Sunny. However, there's a dash of hypnotism in it as well. A lot of backstabbing characters thrown your way too. Oh, and Count Olaf is sort of like Santa, always around.. watching from afar.. and creepy as fuck. <br/><br/>The one thing I didn't like about this book was the child labor. Thank god t</span>
  <span id="freeText11025719072639134107" style="display:none"><i>The Miserable Mill</i> is the fourth installment of <i>A Series of Unfortunate Events</i>. A lot happened in this book and I'm still a little shook from it. <br /><br />Now in this book we still have the three kids: Klaus, Violet, and Sunny. However, there's a dash of hypnotism in it as well. A lot of backstabbing characters thrown your way too. Oh, and Count Olaf is sort of like Santa, always around.. watching from afar.. and creepy as fuck. <br /><br />The one thing I didn't like about this book was the child labor. Thank god there was one smart ass adult, Charlie, because even he noticed that it was wrong to have kids working in the mills. Then the adults trying to take the fortune away from three innocent kids is still messed up in my eyes. The amount of things these three had to deal with in this book sort of blew my mind.<br /><br />Overall, I'm still a little shook. I can't wait to dive into the next book just to see what curve ball these kids are thrown next.</span>

  <span id="freeText13401945296357045297" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5</b><br /><br />I really wanted to love this one because sounded so much more interesting and exciting that all the others but unfortunately I ended up liking it less.<br /><br /><b>The theme of the mill and the hypnosis was so cool at first but the development didn't convince me.</b><br />This book for me <b>had</b> a lot of <b>potential</b> and the idea was super cool, there's a little <b>horror vibe</b> and of course it was kept low and simple and not too much scary because it's meant for kids but <b>the story was a little repetitive throught the book.</b><br /><br /><b>We can barely see and interact with Count Olaf</b> this time and this was one of the aspect that I didn't like.<br />His figure this time is very less present even if the character chosen as his disguise was hilarious. <br /><b>There are a lot of hints since the beginning of the presence of the Count</b>, way more than the other times. <br />This made it a little <b>less exciting to discover who he was or when it would be introduced.</b><br /><br />It was a <b>very fast read</b> and the story <b>overall was fun and enjoyable</b> anyway, well detailed and there are a lot of characters.<br />The book was hard to put down because I just liked the idea so much that I wanted to know what was happening straight away.<br />And I liked that this time there are less "which here means" and there are the explanations made as examples that I found more interesting.<br /><br />Oh and I like that every time at the end there's the little note where there's a little introduction for the next book as well as the title, I love the way it's written.<br /><br /><i>Till the next tragedy ;)</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1568508586264339829">And so another series I started and never got round to finish is returned to. <br/><br/>Carrying on my challenge to finish series I started and some how never got round to finishing I have now started back on the Series of Unfortunate Events. <br/><br/>I think for me there were a few reasons why I lost motivation with this series - the first is the constant reminders of how bad, how unfortunate, now depressing how... (you get the idea) terrible the life of the Baudelaire orphans has got and is yet to get. I underst</span>
  <span id="freeText1568508586264339829" style="display:none">And so another series I started and never got round to finish is returned to. <br /><br />Carrying on my challenge to finish series I started and some how never got round to finishing I have now started back on the Series of Unfortunate Events. <br /><br />I think for me there were a few reasons why I lost motivation with this series - the first is the constant reminders of how bad, how unfortunate, now depressing how... (you get the idea) terrible the life of the Baudelaire orphans has got and is yet to get. I understand its how the author has approached the narrative but it does grate some times. <br /><br />The second is that it feels like it could easily slip in to a formulaic story where each episode is a re-telling of the same premise - over and over again where the children call it out and the authorities first ignore then and then choose to act just a little too late. <br /><br />However book 4 the Miserable Mill shows that is NOT the case - here we are introduced to a new story and one which shows that there is potential for this series to go places I cannot predict or expect - suddenly it has become fresh again. <br /><br />Yes the narrative style is still here however now that I am interested in the story again I am able to tune it out. In short this series deserves a second look. The question is where is it going to go next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1568508586264339829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830375283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10324154671166075848"><i>The Miserable Mill</i> is my favorite in this series so far. Does anybody recall the criminally underrated 1995 film <i>The Mangler</i>? Well, this book is quite similar. When the orphans find themselves at the doors to the creepy Lucky Smells Lumber Mill (what the hell was Lemony Snicket <i>on</i> when he made that name up???), they find that despite the deplorable conditions, at least Count Olaf is nowhere to be seen... but as usual, they can't evade the grim happening in their situation forever.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16056094442106944891" style="display:none">It's been a while since I had time to write a review here on GR since life and college have gotten in the way. Anyway, let's try to get back on track and make life a little brighter with more reading.<br /><br /><i> “Just knowing that they could read made the Baudelaire orphans feel as if their wretched lives could be a little brighter.” </i><br /><br />Another Baudelaire unfortunate life stories. Once again they are put under the ~protection of a terrible guardian; this time, they also have to work in the Miserable Mill. Additionally to the mental abuse known from previous stories, now they are also suffering from physical ones, working several hours a day while starving. <br /><br />As if that was not bad enough, we also face some mind-control tools, lots of bubblegums and even a death in this story. A book in which Lemony Snicket maintains his style, but with a better storyline than the ones before.<br /><br /><i> “I'm sure you have heard it said that appearance does not matter so much and that it is what's on the inside that counts. This is, of course, utter nonsense, because if it were true then people who were good on this inside would never have to comb their hair or take a bath, and the whole world would smell even worse than it already does.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16056094442106944891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271096417" />
    <a title="Larissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4919107-larissa"><img alt="Larissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576508167p2/4919107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271096417?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larissa" href="/user/show/4919107-larissa">Larissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271096417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6128912459652739339">I'm not sure I have adequate words to describe my reaction to this book.<br/><br/>I think I need more time to digest. I feel like I stepped out of the Twilight Zone, and I'm suffering from a rare form of Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder.<br/><br/><b>EDIT</b>: I have now changed my final rating to three stars. After reading book 5, it's become clear to me that the pacing and tone of this book is far too irrepressibly dreary, even for an unhappy story like the Baudelaire's. It felt a lot like being battered by a particularly </span>
  <span id="freeText6128912459652739339" style="display:none">I'm not sure I have adequate words to describe my reaction to this book.<br /><br />I think I need more time to digest. I feel like I stepped out of the Twilight Zone, and I'm suffering from a rare form of Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder.<br /><br /><b>EDIT</b>: I have now changed my final rating to three stars. After reading book 5, it's become clear to me that the pacing and tone of this book is far too irrepressibly dreary, even for an unhappy story like the Baudelaire's. It felt a lot like being battered by a particularly thorny ram over and over again until the last sentence ended. I understand this is an unfortunate story, but ultimately, the relentless pain in this novel detracts from the overall enjoyment.<br /><br />That said, I appreciate <i>The Miserable Mill</i>'s place in this series, and it reads very much like the 'true' start after the episodic nature of the first three books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6128912459652739339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K+laD4Ovg6KB+O2w11tidFjBcu4GpJ8S3kQ7sxSNaiu0itq/AAD0NIMjSgoBsOaRXGMsK7Woh3lqWAskk7H1VA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zYHQNJnaVjZXO+w3SIPXYCL9bQs9a1NVibAhmiSfzLtS4lCEGnUhoFXgS42eaFOFJl8zzo5nSz49rBENo6NTxA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
